USER:
You are analyzing **one block of a longer dialogue** to extract actions.

**ACTION** = An atomic communicative act a speaker **directly performed** in a turn.
- Atomic action = minimal unit of action the speaker directly performed.
  - e.g. "User asks to find a paper about HCI in NLP conferences" → split into "User asks to find a paper about HCI", "User asks to find a paper in NLP conferences".
- Include evidence_quote from the utterance.

**Possible action types** (generate new types if needed):
Accept, Acknowledge, Address, Allow, Analyze, Apologize, Ask,
Challenge, Clarify, Classify, Compare, Complain, Confirm, Connect,
Constrain, Critique, Decide, Define, Delegate, Describe, Draft,
Emphasize, Evaluate, Explain, Feedback, Formalize, Frame, Greet,
Hypothesize, Implement, Include, Infer, Instruct, Invite, Justify,
List, Modify, Observe, Plan, Provide, Qualify, Recommend, Refuse,
Report, Request, State, Suggest, Summarize, Warn

**Role:** **SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER**
  * **SHAPER:** Creates/shapes/revises the goal/requirement by proposing new ideas, new tasks, constraints, alternatives, or directions.
  * **EXECUTOR:** Executes/achieves the desired outcome/goal/requirement (e.g., drafting text, providing requested information, coding, searching, implementing).
  * **OTHER:** Neither SHAPER nor EXECUTOR.

[Turn 0] user: Give me a one-day new york city trip schedule based on below instructions.

Your parents are visiting New York City. They will arrive in the morning and stay for a short trip, and you want to plan a one-day itinerary for them. Think carefully about what would make the trip comfortable and enjoyable for parents, rather than for young tourists. Their hotel is in Manhattan, so please use that as the starting point and keep travel time reasonable. Plan the day from morning to evening, including meals, sightseeing, and breaks.
Your parents’ preferences are as follows:

They prefer a relaxed pace and do not want to walk too much
They enjoy famous landmarks, nice views, and pleasant neighborhoods
They like good food, but would prefer reliable and comfortable places over trendy or overly crowded spots
They would appreciate chances to sit down and rest during the day
Try to balance iconic NYC experiences with a schedule that feels smooth and not tiring

My preference is, I would not like to move long distance, but rather explore compact regions just with walking. For food, I also don't want overly crowded spots, but would like to have some good local foods. I do not care the price of the food. I also would like to include a good cafe in the schedule.

Here is a carefully curated, one-day itinerary designed specifically for your parents. It focuses on the **Midtown to Central Park South corridor**. This area is highly compact, allowing you to see some of New York’s most iconic landmarks with minimal walking, while offering wide sidewalks, plenty of benches, and upscale, comfortable dining establishments where price is secondary to quality and ambiance.

### **Morning: Iconic Views and a Great Cafe**

*   **9:30 AM – Morning Coffee & Pastries at Lodi (Rockefeller Center)**
    *   **What it is:** Start your day at Rockefeller Plaza. Lodi is an elegant, Milanese-inspired cafe right on the plaza. 
    *   **Why it works:** It offers excellent coffee and fresh pastries in a beautiful, comfortable setting. You can sit outside (if the weather is nice) or inside, enjoying the view of the iconic Rockefeller Center without dealing with the chaotic crowds of a typical NYC diner.
*   **10:30 AM – Top of the Rock Observation Deck**
    *   **What it is:** The observatory at the top of Rockefeller Center.
    *   **Why it works:** Instead of the Empire State Building (which can feel cramped), Top of the Rock offers wide-open, glass-paneled viewing decks with plenty of indoor seating. The elevators do all the work, and they will get the best view *of* the Empire State Building and Central Park. *(Tip: Book VIP or timed tickets in advance so your parents don't have to wait in line).*
*   **11:45 AM – St. Patrick’s Cathedral**
    *   **What it is:** The famous neo-Gothic cathedral just across the street on 5th Avenue.
    *   **Why it works:** It requires almost no walking from Rockefeller Center. It is breathtakingly beautiful, and more importantly, there are plenty of pews where your parents can sit, rest, and quietly take in the magnificent architecture and stained glass.

### **Afternoon: Fine Dining and Central Park**

*   **12:30 PM – Lunch at The Modern (Bar Room or Dining Room)**
    *   **What it is:** Located inside the Museum of Modern Art (MoMA) on 53rd Street, just a few blocks walk up 5th Avenue. 
    *   **Why it works:** Since price is not an issue, this is the perfect spot for high-quality local dining. It holds two Michelin stars, but the atmosphere is incredibly spacious, comfortable, and quiet—never rowdy. Request a table overlooking the Abby Aldrich Rockefeller Sculpture Garden for a beautiful, serene view while you eat.
*   **2:30 PM – Leisurely Stroll up 5th Avenue to Central Park**
    *   **What it is:** A slow, 6-block walk up 5th Avenue toward Central Park South. 
    *   **Why it works:** The sidewalks here are wide, flat, and lined with famous storefronts (Bergdorf Goodman, Tiffany & Co.). It’s the quintessential "pleasant neighborhood" stroll. 
*   **3:00 PM – Central Park (The Pond & Gapstow Bridge)**
    *   **What it is:** Enter the park at 59th Street and 5th Avenue.
    *   **Why it works:** You do not need to walk deep into the park to experience its magic. Just steps from the entrance is "The Pond" and the famous Gapstow Bridge. There are dozens of shaded benches here. You can sit together, rest your feet, and watch the horse-drawn carriages go by with the NYC skyline peeking through the trees.

### **Late Afternoon / Evening: Classic NYC Elegance**

*   **4:30 PM – Afternoon Tea or Rest at The Palm Court (The Plaza Hotel)**
    *   **What it is:** The iconic restaurant located in the lobby of The Plaza Hotel, right across the street from your Central Park resting spot.
    *   **Why it works:** This fulfills your cafe/rest requirement perfectly. It is a legendary NYC experience. The seating is plush, the room is stunning (featuring a beautiful stained-glass dome), and it provides a luxurious environment to sit back, use the restroom, and enjoy a pot of premium tea or coffee before dinner.
*   **6:30 PM – Dinner at Marea**
    *   **What it is:** A renowned, high-end Italian and seafood restaurant located right on Central Park South (Columbus Circle). 
    *   **Why it works:** It is a short, flat walk (or a 3-minute taxi ride) from The Plaza. Marea is a staple of upscale NYC dining. The tables are well-spaced, the seating is incredibly comfortable, and the service is highly attentive. It is popular but attracts a refined, quieter crowd, making it very easy for your parents to hear each other and relax after their day.

### **Why this itinerary works for your parents:**
1.  **Compact Footprint:** The entire day takes place between 49th Street and 59th Street. The total walking distance for the *entire day* is under 1.5 miles, broken up into very short 10-to-15-minute segments.
2.  **Built-in Rest:** Every single activity (Lodi, Top of the Rock, St. Patrick's, The Modern, Central Park benches, The Plaza) involves comfortable seating. 
3.  **Crowd Control:** By choosing upscale, well-managed dining venues (The Modern, Marea, The Plaza), you bypass the cramped, noisy environments typical of tourist-heavy areas, giving your parents a premium, stress-free experience.

Here is your revised itinerary. To accommodate a sunset view at the Top of the Rock, I have reversed the geographic flow of the day. You will now start at Central Park in the morning and slowly work your way south down 5th Avenue, ending at Rockefeller Center for sunset and dinner. 

I have also updated the dinner recommendation to **Le Bernardin**, which is widely considered one of the best and most elegant restaurants in New York. It is incredibly comfortable, famously quiet (perfect for conversation), and located just one and a half blocks from Rockefeller Center.

*(Note: Prices below are estimates per person, assuming high-end choices, and include approximate taxes and standard 20% gratuity. Sunset times vary drastically in NYC depending on the month, so you will need to book your Top of the Rock tickets for about 45 minutes before the actual sunset time on your specific date).*

### **Morning: Central Park & A Grand Cafe**

*   **10:00 AM – Central Park (The Pond & Gapstow Bridge)**
    *   **The Plan:** Start your day at the 59th Street & 5th Avenue entrance to Central Park. Walk just a few steps in to see The Pond and Gapstow Bridge. There are plenty of benches here to sit, breathe in the morning air, and look at the skyline.
    *   **Cost:** Free
*   **10:45 AM – Morning Cafe at The Palm Court (The Plaza Hotel)**
    *   **The Plan:** Walk across the street into the lobby of The Plaza Hotel. The Palm Court is a stunning, iconic room with plush seating and a beautiful stained-glass ceiling. It is the perfect, uncrowded spot to enjoy premium coffee, tea, and fresh morning pastries in total comfort.
    *   **Cost:** ~$45 per person (Premium coffee/tea and a pastry/light bite).

### **Midday: 5th Avenue & A Michelin-Starred Lunch**

*   **11:45 AM – Leisurely Stroll down 5th Avenue**
    *   **The Plan:** Walk south down 5th Avenue from 59th Street to 53rd Street. This is a flat, easy 6-block walk past famous window displays like Bergdorf Goodman, Cartier, and Tiffany & Co.
    *   **Cost:** Free
*   **12:30 PM – Lunch at The Modern (Bar Room)**
    *   **The Plan:** Located inside the Museum of Modern Art (53rd St, just off 5th Ave). This is a spectacular, spacious restaurant that offers incredible local ingredients. The Bar Room is slightly more casual than the main dining room but still offers Michelin-starred quality in a very comfortable, well-spaced environment. 
    *   **Cost:** ~$110 per person (Appetizer, main course, non-alcoholic beverage, tax, and tip).

### **Afternoon: Architecture & Pre-Sunset Rest**

*   **2:30 PM – St. Patrick’s Cathedral**
    *   **The Plan:** Walk three blocks south to 50th Street. This breathtaking cathedral offers a quiet, serene environment. Your parents can sit in the pews for as long as they like to rest their legs and admire the architecture.
    *   **Cost:** Free (Donations accepted).
*   **3:30 PM – Afternoon Rest at Lodi (Rockefeller Plaza)**
    *   **The Plan:** Walk one block west to Rockefeller Center. Lodi is a beautiful Milanese-style cafe right on the plaza. This is your designated resting spot before heading up to the observation deck. Sit down, have a sparkling water or an espresso, and enjoy the ground-level view of the plaza.
    *   **Cost:** ~$25 per person (Beverage and a small snack/gelato).

### **Evening: Sunset Views & World-Class Dining**

*   **Sunset – Top of the Rock Observation Deck**
    *   **The Plan:** Head into Rockefeller Center and take the elevator up. **Crucial tip:** Buy the *Express Pass* ticket in advance. This allows you to skip the security, elevator, and sunset queues, which is highly recommended so your parents do not have to stand in line. The glass panels and indoor seating areas make this the most comfortable sunset view in the city.
    *   **Cost:** ~$85 per person (Express Pass ticket).
*   **Post-Sunset – Dinner at Le Bernardin**
    *   **The Plan:** Walk just 1.5 blocks west to 51st Street & 7th Avenue. Le Bernardin holds 3 Michelin stars and is famous for its exquisite seafood. More importantly for your parents, the dining room is incredibly spacious, the seats are luxurious, and the acoustics are designed to be quiet. It is the antithesis of a crowded, trendy tourist trap. 
    *   **Cost:** ~$320 per person (4-course Prix Fixe menu at $210, plus a glass of wine, tax, and tip).

---

### **Estimated Price Breakdown**

Here is the estimated cost based on a party of **3 adults** (You + 2 Parents):

*   **Morning Cafe (The Palm Court):** $45 x 3 = $135
*   **Lunch (The Modern):** $110 x 3 = $330
*   **Afternoon Cafe (Lodi):** $25 x 3 = $75
*   **Top of the Rock (Express Pass):** $85 x 3 = $255
*   **Dinner (Le Bernardin):** $320 x 3 = $960

**Total Estimated Price for the Day (Per Person):** ~$585
**Total Estimated Price for the Day (Party of 3):** ~$1,755

*(Note: If Le Bernardin feels too formal, a fantastic alternative right inside Rockefeller Center is **Limani**, a stunning, highly comfortable Greek seafood restaurant. Dinner there would reduce the evening cost to about $150 per person).*

USER:
You are given ALL actions extracted from a complete dialogue. Your task:
(1) Identify **outcomes** (purpose-linked desired deliverables)
(2) Assign every action to exactly one outcome

Every collaboration has a **purpose**. **Outcomes are purpose-linked desired deliverables** — concrete outputs that participants are actually working toward.

- **Outcomes = purpose-linked desired deliverables:** Deliverables are not limited to text or documents — they can be a **decision**, **advice**, **plan**, **clarification**, or any other concrete result. Do **not** include things only mentioned without being adopted as a goal.
- **Requested or agreed outputs:** Any concrete output a participant **explicitly requests** or participants **agree to produce** is a deliverable.
- **Primary output:** The main thing the dialogue aims to produce must appear as an outcome. Sub-deliverables are children.
- **Phrasing:** e.g. "decision for X", "advice for X", "draft for X", "plan for X".
- **Hierarchy:** **parent** = abstract/general, **child** = specific/concrete. Use parent_outcome_id / child_outcome_ids.
- **Granularity:** Prefer consolidated, task-level outcomes. Example: "Workshop plan (date, venue, agenda)" NOT separate "Decide date", "Decide time", etc.
- **No duplicates.** Each distinct deliverable exactly once.

**REQUIREMENT** = An atomic, externally verifiable SUCCESS CONDITION for an outcome.
- Binary testable (pass/fail).
- Must be explicitly stated or adopted as binding in the dialogue.

**NOT a requirement:** content itself, advice, implementation methods, internal reasoning, example outputs, one-off decisions.

Extract ONLY if ALL pass:
1) NECESSITY — framed as mandatory (must/need/required/cannot, numeric constraints, explicit include/exclude)
2) GROUNDING — directly stated, no inference
3) REPLACEABILITY — cannot be swapped without violating success
4) BINARY TESTABILITY — reviewer can judge pass/fail

Operations:
- **create**: New requirement. Check for revise BEFORE create.
- **revise**: Modify existing requirement (contradicts/tightens/relaxes/replaces). Use EXACT existing req_id in related_to (within this outcome).
- **delete**: Explicitly cancels a previously binding condition.

Edge cases:
- Advice itself is NOT a requirement. Only constraints ON the advice.
- "Try to / ideally / could / maybe" → not binding → not a requirement.

[7-7] Turn 7 (assistant) Confirm: Assistant confirms Avra is within a reasonable distance from Top of the Rock to keep it in the desired zone. [role: EXECUTOR]
[7-8] Turn 7 (assistant) Decide: Assistant re-evaluates the schedule, pins Mozzarella & Vino for lunch, factors in a 7:00 PM sunset, and includes walking times. [role: SHAPER]
[7-9] Turn 7 (assistant) Provide: Assistant provides an updated itinerary that expands Central Park time to 1.5 hours and shifts subsequent activities. [role: EXECUTOR]
[7-10] Turn 7 (assistant) Provide: Assistant includes estimated walking times between each stop in the updated itinerary. [role: EXECUTOR]
[7-12] Turn 7 (assistant) List: Assistant provides detailed time blocks, activity descriptions, walking times, and cost estimates for the full day. [role: EXECUTOR]

**REQUIREMENT** = An atomic, externally verifiable SUCCESS CONDITION for an outcome.
- Binary testable (pass/fail).
- Must be explicitly stated or adopted as binding in the dialogue.

**NOT a requirement:** content itself, advice, implementation methods, internal reasoning, example outputs, one-off decisions.

Extract ONLY if ALL pass:
1) NECESSITY — framed as mandatory (must/need/required/cannot, numeric constraints, explicit include/exclude)
2) GROUNDING — directly stated, no inference
3) REPLACEABILITY — cannot be swapped without violating success
4) BINARY TESTABILITY — reviewer can judge pass/fail

Operations:
- **create**: New requirement. Check for revise BEFORE create.
- **revise**: Modify existing requirement (contradicts/tightens/relaxes/replaces). Use EXACT existing req_id in related_to (within this outcome).
- **delete**: Explicitly cancels a previously binding condition.

Edge cases:
- Advice itself is NOT a requirement. Only constraints ON the advice.
- "Try to / ideally / could / maybe" → not binding → not a requirement.

Return JSON only (bound_outcome_id must be "outcome_5"):

{
  "requirement_ops": [
    {
      "op": "create",
      "req_id": "req_1",
      "bound_outcome_id": "outcome_5",

      "implementation_action_ids": [],
      "related_to": [],
      "explicit_or_implicit": "<explicit|implicit>",
      "rationale": "<why extracted>"
    }
  ]
}

Use action_ids (e.g. "3-1") in creation_action_ids / contributing_action_ids / implementation_action_ids.
CRITICAL: Respond with ONLY the JSON object. No additional text.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

--- Entry 10 ---

--- Entry 11 ---
[5-6] Turn 5 (assistant): Analyze — Assistant says it is weighing different lunch locales and trying to minimize walking distance. (role: SHAPER)

--- Entry 12 ---
[5-14] Turn 5 (assistant): Provide — Assistant provides a full revised itinerary with detailed schedule, locations, and costs. (role: EXECUTOR)


========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

=== SECTION B: SUBSEQUENT ACTIONS (after the requirement, same outcome) ===
These actions occurred AFTER the requirement was created, within the same outcome.
--- Entry 0 ---

--- Entry 1 ---

--- Entry 2 ---

--- Entry 3 ---

--- Entry 4 ---

--- Entry 5 ---

--- Entry 6 ---

--- Entry 7 ---

--- Entry 10 ---

--- Entry 11 ---

--- Entry 12 ---
[5-14] Turn 5 (assistant): Provide — Assistant provides a full revised itinerary with detailed schedule, locations, and costs. (role: EXECUTOR)


========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.
